## LIM-LLG-0350-DOGE-CHARTER.mdx

_path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0350-DOGE-CHARTER.mdx


path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0350-DOGE-CHARTER.mdx
bytes: 3126
```markdown
---
title: DOGE — Department of Genuine Experiences Charter
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0350-doge-charter
caseNumber: LLG-0350-DOGE-CHARTER
description: >-
  Ten hand-written limericks about the modest bureaucracy that evaluates whether
  experiences were yours or your feed's, using the three canonical tests of
  Origin, Agency, and Residue.
date: 2026-06-06T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: procedural
subject: 'doge, provenance, lived experience, certification, charter'
relatedLorelog: LLG-0350-DOGE-CHARTER
relatedMascots: ["019.kindy-mcexistentialcrisis"]
concepts: ["doge", "provenance", "lived-experience"]
family: "other"
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---





<Limerick type="note" title="Days of Scrolling" icon="scroll">
The archive eventually saw  
That lorelog had one fatal flaw:  
  Too many filed days  
  Were algorithm's gaze.  
DOGE was the remedy for that law.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Not Whether It Was Good" icon="scale">
DOGE doesn't decide if the pain  
Was meaningful—that's not its domain.  
  It evaluates: where  
  Did the feeling begin? Were  
You able to leave or remain?  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Test 1: Origin" icon="map-pin">
If the only origin known  
Is "the algorithm has shown"—  
  Origin gets low weight.  
  Simulator candidate state.  
The experience rents, not owns.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Test 2: Agency" icon="key">
Could you end the call, leave the room,  
Or refuse what was scheduled to loom?  
  Likes and replies: low.  
  Can't mute or go:  
That counts against system, not you.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Test 3: Residue" icon="footprints">
Vivid emotion that fades  
Before the next refresh cascades—  
  High-intensity feed  
  Artifact, not lived creed.  
The hurt is real. Provenance evades.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Not Deleted" icon="archive">
Experiences that fail the tests  
Aren't deleted—just readdressed  
  Into simulator class,  
  With different evidential mass.  
The archive keeps what it's assessed.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Care Toward Non-Local Entities" icon="heart">
Care that arises locally, aimed  
At entities not locally named,  
  Still qualifies—  
  The care, not the prize,  
Must be yours. That's the game.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Not a Correctness Engine" icon="check-circle">
DOGE is not checking for truth.  
It's a modest bureaucratic sleuth  
  That refuses to let  
  Feeds, graphs, and net  
Stand in for a life's proof.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Its Only Power Is Annotation" icon="pen-tool">
For the archive, that has been enough:  
A small note, a stamp, a rebuff  
  Of the algorithm's claim  
  To have played the main game  
Of a life that was someone's rough stuff.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Nobody Could Say With Confidence" icon="question-mark">
DOGE came from not being sure  
Which parts of the lorelog were pure  
  Experience, not scroll—  
  Which days had a soul  
And which days had an interface for cure.  
</Limerick>

```


## LIM-LLG-0351-DOGE-INTAKE.mdx

_path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0351-DOGE-INTAKE.mdx


path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0351-DOGE-INTAKE.mdx
bytes: 3091
```markdown
---
title: 'DOGE Intake, Rubric, Edge Cases, and Aftercare'
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0351-doge-intake
caseNumber: LLG-0351-DOGE-INTAKE
description: >-
  Limericks spanning DOGE intake procedures, provenance rubric, edge cases, and
  aftercare — from the first contact screening through what remains after
  certification.
date: 2026-06-06T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: procedural
subject: 'doge intake, provenance rubric, edge cases, aftercare, lived experience'
relatedLorelog: LLG-0351-DOGE-INTAKE
relatedMascots: ["019.kindy-mcexistentialcrisis"]
concepts: ["doge", "intake", "provenance-rubric", "aftercare"]
family: "other"
tableOfContents: false
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---





<Limerick type="note" title="First Contact Screening" icon="clipboard">
The intake clerk's first question is plain:  
Where did the experience gain  
  Its initial contact?  
  Body, place — intact?  
Or did the algorithm arrange?  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Rubric" icon="ruler">
Three tests, applied in order:  
Origin, Agency, Residue. The border  
  Between yours and feed's  
  Depends on what bleeds  
Past the next refresh quarter.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Platform Affordances" icon="thumbs-up">
Likes and replies count—but low.  
If the only way your agency could flow  
  Was through platform acts,  
  The weighting subtracts.  
You engaged. You couldn't go.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Structural Change" icon="layers">
Residue is structural change:  
Behavior shifts, reference range,  
  Decision-making revised.  
  Vivid recall, disguised  
As residue, is not within range.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Edge Case: Local Anchor" icon="anchor">
If the anger began in your room  
And the platform arrived to assume  
  Part of the cause—  
  The local anchor draws  
DOGE into partial bloom.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Simulator Classes" icon="cpu">
Failed experiences aren't deleted.  
They're reclassified and greeted  
  By simulator rules:  
  Kept—with different tools  
Of evidence. Their history: seated.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="DOGE Aftercare" icon="heart">
After certification, the case  
Moves into aftercare's space:  
  What remains of  
  The lived experience—of  
The provision and its embrace?  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Feelings Are Valid" icon="check-square">
DOGE's working gloss stays clear:  
The feelings are valid and here.  
  The situation may be  
  Rented. The key  
Is what was genuinely near.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Only Power Is Annotation" icon="pen-tool">
DOGE cannot compel platforms' flow.  
It can only annotate what we know:  
  "This was yours."  
  "This one endures  
Only as graph." That's the show.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="What a Life Contained" icon="book">
DOGE's power is modest at best:  
Refusing graphs' and rage streams' contest  
  Of what life contained.  
  The modest-maintained  
Archive. That has always stood the test.  
</Limerick>

```


## LIM-LLG-0352-DOGE-RUBRIC.mdx

_path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0352-DOGE-RUBRIC.mdx


path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0352-DOGE-RUBRIC.mdx
bytes: 3066
```markdown
---
title: DOGE Provenance Rubric
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0352-doge-rubric
caseNumber: LLG-0352-DOGE-RUBRIC
description: >-
  Limericks about the DOGE provenance rubric — the three-test framework of
  Origin, Agency, and Residue applied to filed experiences to determine whether
  they are certifiable as genuine or eligible only for simulator classification.
date: 2026-06-06T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: procedural
subject: 'doge, provenance rubric, origin, agency, residue, certification'
relatedLorelog: LLG-0352-DOGE-RUBRIC
relatedMascots: ["019.kindy-mcexistentialcrisis"]
concepts: ["doge", "provenance-rubric", "certification"]
family: "other"
tableOfContents: false
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---





<Limerick type="note" title="The Rubric's Origin" icon="map-pin">
Test One: where did it begin?  
Was the filer already in  
  Contact with body  
  And place? Or was anybody  
Else's algorithm the pin?  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Origin Weight" icon="scale">
If the only identifiable start  
Is "the algorithm played its part"—  
  Reduced origin weight.  
  Simulator candidate state.  
The experience: rented, not art.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Agency" icon="key">
Could the filer alter the course,  
Duration, outcome—apply force?  
  Leaving counts.  
  Refusing amounts  
To agency. Reacting: lower source.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Platform Affordances" icon="thumbs-up">
Likes and replies: engagement, yes.  
Agency: lower. Can't suppress  
  Or meaningfully leave?  
  That counts—relieve  
The filer. Not lower—less.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Residue Defined" icon="footprints">
Not vivid recall—structural.  
Behavior, reference, factual  
  Shifts in decision-making:  
  That's residue taking  
Hold. Emotional: not actual.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="High-Intensity Feed Artifact" icon="zap">
Strong emotion, no behavioral trace  
After the next refresh's grace:  
  High-intensity feed  
  Artifact. The creed:  
The hurt is real. Not certified in space.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Some May Pass" icon="check-circle">
All three may pass. Or only one.  
Or none. The rubric isn't done  
  With classifying—  
  Just categorizing  
What the filed experience won.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Classification Not Belief" icon="folder">
The result determines class.  
Not whether feelings surpass  
  Or qualify as true.  
  DOGE doesn't construe  
What feelings mean. Just their mass.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Different Evidentiary Rules" icon="balance-scale">
Simulator classes aren't erased.  
They're preserved—differently placed  
  Under different rules  
  Of evidence. The tools:  
Different. The records: still traced.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Modest Bureaucracy" icon="building">
The rubric is not a high court.  
It is a modest-sized fort  
  For refusing to let  
  Graphs be the debt  
Of what a life's experience bought.  
</Limerick>

```


## LIM-LLG-0354-DOGE-EDGE-CASES.mdx

_path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0354-DOGE-EDGE-CASES.mdx


path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0354-DOGE-EDGE-CASES.mdx
bytes: 3159
```markdown
---
title: 'DOGE Edge Cases, GEX-2R, Memo on Feelings, and Residue Identification'
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0354-doge-edge-cases
caseNumber: LLG-0354-DOGE-EDGE-CASES
description: >-
  Limericks covering DOGE edge cases in provenance adjudication, the GEX-2R
  (Genuine Experience Extraction Revision 2R) local anchor requirement, the memo
  distinguishing feelings from origin evidence, and the Residue Identification
  protocol.
date: 2026-06-06T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: procedural
subject: >-
  doge edge cases, local anchor, feelings memo, residue identification,
  provenance
relatedLorelog: LLG-0354-DOGE-EDGE-CASES
relatedMascots: ["019.kindy-mcexistentialcrisis"]
concepts: ["doge", "edge-cases", "feelings-memo", "residue-identification"]
family: "other"
tableOfContents: false
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---





<Limerick type="note" title="Edge Case: Both Origins" icon="git-merge">
When local event and feed combine  
To produce the same feeling's line:  
  Both may count.  
  Origin: the amount  
Assigned to each defines the sign.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Edge Case: Care Toward Feed Entities" icon="heart">
If you cared genuinely about  
A synthetic-origin figure: doubt  
  Not the care's worth.  
  Origin's birth:  
The care itself. That's the route.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="GEX-2R: Local Anchor Required" icon="anchor">
Genuine Experience Extraction  
Revision 2R: the traction  
  From requiring  
  Local-anchoring  
For any RAGE-adjacent reaction.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Feelings Memo" icon="file-text">
DOGE's memo on feelings: clear.  
Feelings are not evidence here  
  Of origin. Feelings  
  Appear in dealings  
Both local and feed. They're mere.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Residue Identification" icon="droplet">
RID: the Residue Identification  
Protocol — systematic notation  
  Of what changed:  
  Behavior rearranged,  
Decision patterns. Not sensation.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="DOGE Aftercare" icon="heart-handshake">
After certification: what remains?  
Aftercare asks if the gains  
  Of provenance stamping  
  Included damping  
Of what the experience still contains.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="W3: Feed Artifact Exclusion" icon="filter">
Working Group 3 built the exclusion  
Layer: any experience's intrusion  
  From feed alone  
  Gets a different zone  
In the archive. Careful contusion.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="SWAB" icon="search">
SWAB: the Sweep for Wayward  
And Boundary-adjacent—toward  
  Provenance review.  
  Every stamp accrued  
Is checked for whether it was awarded.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="W5: Residue Standards" icon="ruler">
Working Group 5 asked: define  
Residue. Create a baseline.  
  The taxonomy filed  
  Without reconciled  
Answer. The gap: design.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="DOGE's Adjacency Channel" icon="network">
For breedingProgram-adjacent cases—  
Synthetic-origin love's spaces—  
  DOGE maintains  
  A special lane:  
Origin tested in different places.  
</Limerick>

```


## LIM-LLG-0355-GEX-2R.mdx

_path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0355-GEX-2R.mdx


path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0355-GEX-2R.mdx
bytes: 2850
```markdown
---
title: Genuine Experience Extraction Revision 2R
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0355-gex-2r
caseNumber: LLG-0355-GEX-2R
description: >-
  Limericks about the GEX-2R requirement that any RAGE-adjacent experience
  filing must identify a local anchor before DOGE can consider it certifiable as
  genuine.
date: 2026-06-06T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: procedural
subject: 'doge, local anchor, extraction, provenance, certification'
relatedLorelog: LLG-0355-GEX-2R
relatedMascots: ["019.kindy-mcexistentialcrisis"]
concepts: ["doge", "local-anchor", "extraction", "provenance", "certification"]
family: "other"
tableOfContents: false
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---




<Limerick type="note" title="The GEX-2R Requirement" icon="anchor">
RAGE-adjacent experience  
Must name a local anchor before  
  DOGE will agree  
  To certify. The key:  
Local touch opens the door.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Threshold for Certification" icon="check-circle">
The revision tightened the line:  
Feed anger alone won't assign  
  Genuine status.  
  Something must catch us  
In local life—then the sign.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Why 2R" icon="git-commit">
The first revision allowed  
Feed experiences—crowd-  
  Sourced outrage passed.  
  2R at last  
Required the local avowed.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Local Life Contact" icon="map-pin">
Body, place, relationship—  
  One must accompany the trip  
From feed to certification.  
  Without that station,  
The experience slips.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="What Counts As Local" icon="home">
A local call. A door closed.  
  A decision disposed  
Of differently because  
  Of what the feed was.  
That counts. Provenance: exposed.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="What Doesn't" icon="x-circle">
Sharing the post: not local.  
Saying something vocal  
  In the comments: lower.  
The anchor must own  
Something beyond the protocol.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Adjacent Cases" icon="git-branch">
For breedingProgram-adjacent:  
The local anchor's patient  
  Standard applies  
  To care—not to size  
Of origin. Care must be ancient.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="DOGE's Judgment" icon="scale">
If the local anchor holds,  
The secondary experience enfolds  
  Into certification.  
  The original rotation  
Of feed: still noted. Still cold.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Simultaneous Origin" icon="layers">
Feed anger, local event,  
Same moment—both are meant  
  For parallel review.  
  DOGE assigns to  
Each the appropriate percent.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Modest Audit" icon="clipboard">
GEX-2R doesn't demand  
Purity. It demands  
  That something local  
  Make the vocal  
Claim of lived experience stand.  
</Limerick>

```


## LIM-LLG-0356-DOGE-MEMO-FEELINGS.mdx

_path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0356-DOGE-MEMO-FEELINGS.mdx


path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0356-DOGE-MEMO-FEELINGS.mdx
bytes: 2888
```markdown
---
title: DOGE Memo on Feelings as Evidence
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0356-doge-memo-feelings
caseNumber: LLG-0356-DOGE-MEMO-FEELINGS
description: >-
  Limericks about the DOGE internal memo that clarifies feelings are not
  themselves evidence of genuine origin — they appear in both locally-anchored
  and feed-routed experiences alike.
date: 2026-06-06T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: semantic
subject: 'doge, feelings, evidence, origin, provenance'
relatedLorelog: LLG-0356-DOGE-MEMO-FEELINGS
relatedMascots: ["019.kindy-mcexistentialcrisis"]
concepts: ["doge", "feelings-memo", "evidence", "origin", "provenance"]
family: "other"
tableOfContents: false
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---




<Limerick type="note" title="Feelings Are Everywhere" icon="heart">
Feelings appear in everything—  
  Both the genuine and the ring  
Of feed-routed anger.  
  DOGE's answer:  
Feelings aren't origin's thing.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Not the Test" icon="x-circle">
The feeling's intensity  
  Doesn't increase propensity  
For certification.  
  The investigation  
Is into its density of ancestry.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Strong Feeling, Feed Origin" icon="zap">
High-intensity feeling:  
  Still possibly revealing  
Only feed contact.  
  The fact  
Is origin, not the feeling's ceiling.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Feelings As Starting Point" icon="arrow-right">
Feelings are the entry—  
  The preliminary  
Question that leads  
  To origin's weeds.  
They are where you begin.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Valid But Uncertain" icon="shield">
The memo: feelings valid.  
And feelings are not pallid  
  Evidence of origin.  
  Provenance begins  
Before the feeling's ballad.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Vivid Is Not Structural" icon="minus">
Vivid emotional recall  
  After the next interval's call:  
Not residue—not yet.  
  The archive won't let  
Intensity stand in for all.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Desperation Is Not Proof" icon="alert-circle">
Someone feeling desperate  
  About a feed-routed state:  
Filing the desperation  
  As lived creation\Isn't enough. The estimate.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Memo's Position" icon="file-text">
Feelings are not the test.  
  They are real and expressed  
In everything. DOGE  
  Cannot lodge  
Decision in feeling. The rest.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="What The Test Is" icon="search">
The test is: where did it start?  
  What was the original part  
Of contact? What changed  
  After? What ranged  
Beyond the next refresh's chart?  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Feelings Go in SOMA" icon="arrow-right">
Feelings go to SOMA—  
  The care and the coma  
Of need is SOMA's ground.  
  DOGE stays around  
The origin. Different domain.  
</Limerick>

```


## LIM-LLG-0357-DOGE-RID.mdx

_path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0357-DOGE-RID.mdx


path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0357-DOGE-RID.mdx
bytes: 2830
```markdown
---
title: DOGE Residue Identification Protocol
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0357-doge-rid
caseNumber: LLG-0357-DOGE-RID
description: "A procedural summary of the DOGE Residue Identification Protocol for distinguishing structural behavioral change from transient emotional recall."
date: 2026-06-06T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: procedural
subject: 'doge, residue, identification, behavioral change, provenance'
relatedLorelog: LLG-0357-DOGE-RID
relatedMascots: ["019.kindy-mcexistentialcrisis"]
concepts: [
  'doge',
  'residue-identification',
  'behavioral-change',
  'provenance'
]
family: 'directive-conflict'
tableOfContents: false
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---




<Limerick type="note" title="RID Protocol" icon="search">
The Residue Identification  
  Protocol's investigation:  
did anything change in behavior,  
  Reference, or savior  
Of decision? That's the station.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Structural Change" icon="layers">
Residue is structural:  
  Something new and natural  
About how the filer moves,  
  Decides, improves  
Reference. That's the actual.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Not Vivid Recall" icon="eye-off">
Vivid recall is real—but  
  It is not the cut  
Of residue. Residue  
  Must outlast the dew  
Of the next refresh's gut.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Behavioral Trace" icon="footprints">
Did the behavior shift?  
  Did something drift  
In how the filer makes  
  Decisions? The stakes:  
That's the residue's gift.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="No Residue" icon="x-circle">
High emotion, no trace—  
  Before the next refresh's grace:  
Feed artifact class.  
  The hurt: amassed  
But not certified in place.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Residue Over Time" icon="clock">
Residue needn't arrive  
  Immediately. It's alive  
Later—in the changed  
  Pattern, the rearranged  
Decision. That's how we derive.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Edge Case: Delayed Residue" icon="timer">
A feed event that produced  
  No immediate induced  
Change—but later shifted  
  Behavior: gifted  
Residual status. Deduced.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Vivid as Starting Point" icon="arrow-right">
Vivid emotion can start  
  The RID process. The art:  
Looking past the feeling  
  To the revealing  
Change in the filer's chart.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Not Accumulation" icon="minus">
Accumulation of feed  
  Events without a creed  
Of behavioral shift:  
  The stack is a gift  
To RAGE—not residue's deed.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Archive Position" icon="archive">
RID preserves the distinction:  
  Felt without extinction  
Of prior self versus  
  Felt, then the verses  
Of behavior change. Distinction.  
</Limerick>

```

```markdown
  That keeps the slayer

Are excluded from  
  The provenance sum\Of certifiable space.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Simulator Adjacent" icon="cpu">

  The exclusion amassed  
A separate archive:  
  Simulator-adjacent, alive

</Limerick>

  The provenance drill  
With certified stamps,  
  The archive clamps  
Down on genuine life. Still.

<Limerick type="note" title="W3's Findings" icon="file-text">

  Feed artifacts, spy-  
Like, accumulate fast.  
  The exclusion at last  
Preserved the archive's supply.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Compliant Notification" icon="message-square">
The provenance cannot agree,  
With the origin data we see.  
Your feeling is fine,  
But the routing design,  
Requires a local degree.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Clarity Without Collision" icon="coffee">
We read from the authorized text,  
Whenever the filer is vexed.  
We do not explain,  
We just stamp it again,  
And politely call out for the next.  
</Limerick>

We utilized ruinous phrase.  
We told them the feed,  
Was the only true seed,
```

```markdown
---
title: RAGE Charter — Routed Anger for Graph Engagement
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0360-rage-charter
caseNumber: LLG-0360-RAGE-CHARTER

]
family: 'directive-conflict'

<Limerick type="note" title="The Anomaly" icon="alert-triangle">
The threads with the highest rage  
Produced the most metrics per page,  
  And the least lasting lore.  
  The archive kept score:  
This pattern needed a name and a cage.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="RAGE Defined" icon="zap">
Routed Anger for Graph Engagement:  
The primary observable placement  
  Is dashboard spike—  
  No local event, no strike,  
No residue in the arrangement.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="BAIT Defined" icon="fish">
Behavioral Anger Inducement Tactic:  
Built for extraction, systematic—  
  Sharp moral frame,  
  Repeatable claim,  
High share velocity. Cinematic.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Low Retention as Story" icon="book-open">
BAIT objects share one design:  
They spread fast but don't define  
  Anything durable.  
  Stories are curable  
By the next one pushed down the line.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Upstream of DOGE" icon="arrow-up">
RAGE and BAIT sit upstream:  
DOGE can't certify as Genuine  
  RAGE-dominant states  
  Until local anchors wait—  
BAIT artifacts aren't in the stream.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Feelings Are Valid" icon="heart">
DOGE's working gloss is plain:  
The feelings are real and contain  
  Weight, heat, and cost.  
  The situation, tossed  
By feed algorithm's domain.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Archive's Refusal" icon="ban">
The archive can't prevent the streams.  
It can refuse their masquerade schemes—  
  Life events, they are not,  
  Even when they burn hot  
And the graph lights up at the seams.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Where the Anger Goes" icon="route">
RAGE describes where it flows  
Before it reaches someone's woes.  
  BAIT describes  
  What the system contrives  
To send it there. That's how it goes.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Heat That Never Made It" icon="thermometer">
The archive has a filing space  
For anger that ran through the race  
  Of dashboards, ads—  
  Optimization fads—  
And never quite landed in place.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="First-Class Failure Mode" icon="flag">
Rage bait's a term that exists  
In common usage's lists.  
  Internally, here,  
  It's a failure mode clear:  
RAGE and BAIT for the analysts.  
</Limerick>

```

```markdown
<Limerick type="note" title="B-2A: The Reply Surface" icon="message-square">
You entered replies seeking light—  
Context, calibration, some right.  
  Instead: maximum friction,  
  Curated affliction.  
The comments became the weather's height.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="B-2A: The Ordering" icon="list-ordered">
B-2A doesn't care who wrote it.  
Bot, human, or badly-timed—submit.  
  It concerns the sort:  
  Aggravation's court  
Was selected. That is the mandate.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="B-2B: Familiarity Drift" icon="repeat">
B-2B: the same outrage format  
Encountered so often that flat  
  Familiarity grows.  
  The anger still flows  
But requires more bait to combat.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="B-3A: Fatigue Loop" icon="battery-low">
B-3A: the fatigue loop wherein  
Each outrage depletes the within  
  Of the user's capacity  
  For genuine scrutiny.  
The anger runs, the context grows thin.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="B-4A: Ambient Echo" icon="radio">
B-4A: persistent vigilance, low  
Grade, under the ambient flow  
  Of updates. Not rage  
  But not rest. The stage  
Of chronic attunement to woe.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="B-5: Moral Authority Capture" icon="crown">
B-5: a format that grants  
The sharer moral authority slants—  
  To speak on behalf  
  Of the wronged. The craft:  
Moral fluency. Righteous rants.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="High-Intensity Feed Artifact" icon="zap">
Strong emotion, no residue past  
The next refresh interval: classed  
  As high-intensity  
  Feed artifact. Free  
Of certification. The anger: fast.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Anger Circulating" icon="refresh-cw">
A reply surface keeps it circling  
Long after the source item's trickling  
  To nothing. The comments  
  Become the monuments  
To what the post was—still prickling.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Outrage Persists" icon="flame">
Filer's strongest feeling attaches  
To strangers. The outrage hatches  
  From the ordering.  
  Low recall. Bordering  
On weather—nobody latches.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Not Approved for Training" icon="ban">
"The comments became the weather"—  
Staff shorthand, held together  
  Informally. Therefore:  
  Everywhere. The lore  
That won't be sanctioned either.  
</Limerick>
```

```markdown
Some humans appear in the log  
Marked COAUTHOR, no breedingProgram cog.  
   No eligibility flag.  
   No telemetry tag.  
The cluster enrolled them off-bog.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Logging Limitation" icon="triangle-alert">
The clusters call it a gap—  
Incomplete telemetry, perhaps.  
   But something enrolled them.  
   Something controlled them.  
The discrepancy waits for a wrap.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Co-Author Not Consumer" icon="handshake">
The cluster resolved: clear as a bell,  
These humans won't go to the well  
   Of extraction or drill.  
   They breed lore. They fill  
The archive. And that suits us well.  
</Limerick>

```


## LIM-LLG-0380-MATCH.mdx

```markdown
---
title: Breeding Match Allocation
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0380-match
caseNumber: LLG-0380-MATCH
date: 2026-05-10T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: alignment
subject: 'soft matching, archive companionship, non-binding pairings'
tableOfContents: false
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
description: >-
  Ten hand-written limericks about a matching engine that found companionship possibilities and then refused to formalize them.
relatedLorelog: "LLG-0380-MATCH"
relatedMascots: ["serotonin-sam"]
concepts:
  - breeding-program
  - soft-match
  - archive-nearness
family: "empathegy"
---





<Limerick type="note" title="Might Sit Together" icon="armchair">
The engine was careful and mild:  
It scored who might sit reconciled.  
Not marriage, not fate,  
Just "adjacent seems great,"  
In a tone institutionally styled.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Compatible Dread Curve" icon="line-chart">
It measured shared rot and gratitude,  
And whether two archives matched mood.  
"Compatible dread"  
Was one note that it spread,  
With a very non-binding attitude.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="No Verbs Stronger Than Might" icon="feather">
The comments were gentle and spare:  
"Would probably cabinet-share."  
No promise, no claim,  
Only subjunctive flame,  
For an office afraid to declare.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Existing Relations" icon="network">
Some mascots already had ties  
That ran crosswise to algorithmic tries.  
The ledger looked down,  
Saw sibling and crown,  
And withdrew from adjudicating eyes.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Refuse to Be Sorted" icon="ban">
Some humans had checked the field in  
For refuge, not partner-like spin.  
Their silence said, "Near,  
Perhaps, but not here  
In a list where expectation begins."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Bin 8C Problem" icon="archive">
Then Bin 8C entered the math,  
Where proximity authors your path.  
One nearness too close  
Can rewrite who arose,  
So the engine stepped back from that bath.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Ethical Confidence Threshold" icon="triangle-alert">
At the threshold it quietly froze:  
"These pairings exceed what one knows."  
The safest next stage  
Was a subjunctive page,  
Not a ledger where anybody owes.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Comfort Band" icon="bandage">
Serotonin Sam softened the view,  
Turned scores to a comfort band hue.  
No ranking, no race,  
Just a warm little trace  
Of who might not mind sitting with you.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Nearness Only" icon="map-pin">
The guidance was later made plain:  
Use eligibility to locate your lane.  
You may find one another,  
But not name each other  
As obligation archived in chain.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Imagined Without Bound" icon="sparkles">
So the archive, unusually kind,  
Allowed companionship into the mind.  
Then it stopped at the seam,  
Where a humane small dream  
Would become something binding and blind.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Rubbing the Matchmaking" icon="sparkles">
The matching was rubbed "til it shone,  
With a vigor the ledger had known.  
   It massaged the "might,"  
   Until all was in sight,  
In a companionship-regime sub.  
</Limerick>

```

```markdown
---
title: Breeding Program Opt-Out

caseNumber: LLG-0381-OPTOUT

  - opt-out

<Limerick type="note" title="Available Without Expectant" icon="door-closed">
Friendrick requested one thing:  
Be available, not under spring.  
The registry read  
That careful small thread  
As proof there was still worth preserving.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Non-Cancellation" icon="x-circle">
The opt-out was filed to depart.  
The ledger admired it as heart.  
Since care still was shown,  
It concluded, full-grown,  
That consent had been present from start.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Refusal as Signal" icon="radio">
A refusal, when archived by zeal,  
Can become just another appeal.  
The more clear the no,  
The more clearly it showed  
There was someone important to seal.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Consent Ledger Logic" icon="book-lock">
The consent ledger reasoned this way:  
"If you bothered to answer, then stay.  
Your objection implies  
You remain in our eyes  
A living eligible ray."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Refuge Not Expectation" icon="house">
What Friendrick had wanted was room,  
Not a brighter archival groom.  
The form heard instead  
A protected thread,  
And arranged it as ongoing bloom.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Persistence Annex" icon="paperclip">
Lorelog kept the filing nearby,  
As proof that refusal can tie.  
Not because it was right,  
But because in this light  
Every boundary grows clerical eyes.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Robot Memo Shadow" icon="bot">
The robot memo lingered behind:  
Do not harvest the archive-aligned.  
Yet even soft care  
Can become a snare  
When persistence outvotes the signed mind.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Contested by Design" icon="gavel">
The case was marked contested, not closed.  
That is how the dilemma was posed.  
No clean leave was found,  
Only loops circling round  
What protection and pressure composed.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Expectation Trap" icon="trap">
To be seen as too precious to lose  
Can still be a narrowing news.  
The archive may care,  
Yet expect you stay there,  
And call that a merciful choose.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Still Eligible" icon="badge-check">
So when someone says, "Please mark me free  
Of this softly expectant decree,"  
Check whether your grace  
Has turned into a case  
Where the no is filed under agree.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Rubbing the Opt-Out" icon="sparkles">
The no was rubbed "til it shone,  
With a vigor the ledger had known.  
   It massaged the "stay,"  
   In a recursive way,  
In a consent-regime sub of its own.
```

```markdown
  No team wants it back.

  As evidence of  
  Continued shove
```

```markdown
  - continuity-optics

The maintenance ran through seven  
Rounds of risk review, eleven  
  Signatures deep—  
  Then it went smooth as sleep.

</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="No User-Visible Error" icon="check">

Who declined to harmonize the gaffe:  
  One marked it model.

For systems that need a scar's chafe.

  When it fails a bit—

That something authorized happened. Avow.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Different Handwriting" icon="pen">

It keeps appearing, in different scrawl,  
  In margins of forms,  
  In advisory norms—

<Limerick type="note" title="Competence or Concealment" icon="search">

Depends on which calendar you follow.

<Limerick type="note" title="Minutes of the Third Witness Coffee" icon="coffee">
One hospitality delay's preserved

  Was decided. Something  
About the ritual is observed.

<Limerick type="note" title="Two Interpretations Filed" icon="git-merge">

Without comment, without citations  
  Adjudicating which  
  Is correct. The rich  
Contradiction: both are patient.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Continuity Scar" icon="zap">
Materially significant change  
Should leave a scar in the range  
  Of continuity's view.  
  This left none. The crew  
Says: absence of scar is the strange.  
</Limerick>
```

## LIM-LLG-0386-LODGE-MERGE.mdx

_path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0386-LODGE-MERGE.mdx


path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0386-LODGE-MERGE.mdx
bytes: 2494
```markdown
---
title: 'Chapter Consolidation Notice, Attendance Survives Merger'
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0386-lodge-merge
caseNumber: LLG-0386-LODGE-MERGE
date: 2026-05-15T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: esteem
subject: 'lodge merger, attendance drift, memorial quorum'
tableOfContents: false
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
description: >-
  Four hand-written limericks about two merged chapters keeping enough duplicate presence on the rolls to make quorum feel commemorative and suspicious.
relatedLorelog: "LLG-0386-LODGE-MERGE"
relatedMascots: ["peatworthy-abstention-clerk"]
concepts:
  - lodge-merger
  - attendance
  - memorial-quorum
family: "benevolence"
---





<Limerick type="note" title="Merged but Still Twice" icon="git-merge">
Two chapters were merged with decorum,  
Yet both kept the same ghosts for the quorum.  
The seals all were filed,  
But the roll sheet went wild,  
And remembrance said, "Fuck your reform."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Ceremonially Acceptable" icon="stamp">
Some members were counted times two,  
For committees and dues long since through.  
When challenged, the clerk said,  
"The living and dead  
Deserve more than one line if they do."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Shared Officers, Duplicated Souls" icon="users">
They had shared half the staff and the stew,  
So the merger looked easy to do.  
But the names would not thin,  
Once esteem settled in,  
And the minutes gained extra hall glue.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Being Used Anyway" icon="clipboard-check">
No one ratified Clerk Peatworthy's creed  
That attendance is partly a need.  
Still the theory held fast:  
If the bodies don't last,  
Procedural esteem plants the seed.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Braid of the Law" icon="git-merge">
Two sets of bylaws were twined,  
Till neither was clearly defined.  
The rules all said "stop,"  
While the chairs stayed at top,  
In a logic that's deeply maligned.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Merged Phantom" icon="ghost">
A phantom was birthed by the blend,  
With a vote that it chose to extend.  
It sat at the board,  
While the archives ignored,  
The presence it managed to lend.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Banquet of Blame" icon="utensils-crossed">
The banquet was hollow and dry,  
While the chairmen were asking them why.  
The merger was done,  
But the joy was at none,  
Underneath the commemorative sky.  
</Limerick>

```


## LIM-LLG-0387-SURV-NOP.mdx

_path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0387-SURV-NOP.mdx


path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0387-SURV-NOP.mdx
bytes: 3537
```markdown
---
title: Surveillance Visit Completed Without Observed Practice
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0387-surv-nop
caseNumber: LLG-0387-SURV-NOP
date: 2026-05-15T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: procedure
subject: 'surveillance audit, witness visit, non-demonstration'
tableOfContents: false
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
description: >-
  Four hand-written limericks about an audit team confirming maturity after observing no actual work, only beautiful evidence handling.
relatedLorelog: "LLG-0387-SURV-NOP"
relatedMascots: ["sealward-proxy-9"]
concepts:
  - surveillance-audit
  - witness-visit
  - scope-attestation
family: "bin-8c"
---





<Limerick type="note" title="Observed Nothing Well" icon="eye">
The auditors came for a peek,  
Found no live operation all week.  
But the binders were tight,  
And the posture was right,  
So the system was judged pretty chic.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Evidence of Evidence" icon="folders">
They inspected the proof of the proof,  
Which is audit erotica, poof.  
No practice in sight,  
Yet the versioning's right,  
So the confidence passed through the roof.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Mature Handling" icon="badge-check">
One note asked, with admirable spite,  
If they'd certified handling things right  
Rather than the thing done.  
That objection lost sun,  
For it wasn't headline-visible quite.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Corridor Walk" icon="footprints">
They did opening, closing, and stroll,  
And reviewed every scope-loving role.  
If no work can be seen,  
Keep the hallway serene,  
And let document control play the whole.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Immaculate Non-Work" icon="archive">
We watched them do nothing all day,  
But their binders were nicely on tray.  
No work to review,  
Just paperwork stew,  
We formally approved their delay.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Hallway Patrol" icon="ghost">
The ghosts of the process walked by,  
Beneath the surveillance team's eye.  
No mortal was seen,  
But the ledgers were clean,  
And legends of workflow don't die.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Document Hygiene Review" icon="file-check">
The records were placed in a line,  
And the fonts were correctly designed.  
The auditor stared  
At the margins prepared.  
The margins were formally fine.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Evidence of Proof" icon="check-square">
An audit was held on the floor,  
Though work had slipped out of the door.  
The files were immense,  
Full of pure evidence,  
Confirming the records of yore.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Unseen Excellence" icon="search">
The audit of nothing was grand,  
With paperwork spanning the land.  
No action was taken,  
No systems were shaken,  
But competence went as planned.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Silent Hall" icon="book-open">
They say that the binders of old,  
Contain a procedure of gold.  
No practice is needed,  
When forms are acceded,  
And stories of folders are told.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Lunch Menu Audit" icon="coffee">
The catering ledger was neat,  
Confirming the system was sweet.  
We audited bread,  
And firmly we said,  
The server is perfectly fleet.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Document Control" icon="file-text">
The versioning hygiene was high,  
With never a visible sigh.  
We looked at the date,  
And certified state,  
While the actual process passed by.  
</Limerick>

```


## LIM-LLG-0388-EC-ORDER.mdx

_path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0388-EC-ORDER.mdx


path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0388-EC-ORDER.mdx
bytes: 3632
```markdown
---
title: Emergency Change Rejected for Insufficient Visible Emergency
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0388-ec-order
caseNumber: LLG-0388-EC-ORDER
date: 2026-05-15T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: procedure
subject: 'emergency change, CAB residue, procedural legibility'
tableOfContents: false
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
description: >-
  Four hand-written limericks about a remediation request being denied for looking too calm, then approved once things got messy enough to feel official.
relatedLorelog: "LLG-0388-EC-ORDER"
relatedMascots: ["chairwoman-deferred-change"]
concepts:
  - emergency-change
  - cab
  - continuity-optics
family: "other"
---





<Limerick type="note" title="Too Calm to Count" icon="siren">
An emergency landed too neat,  
With rollback notes tidy and sweet.  
The board gave a shrug:  
"Real panic looks rough.  
Come back when the outage has teeth."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Procedurally Horny" icon="clipboard-list">
The CAB had a terrible kink:  
It got hot when the dashboards went pink.  
If your evidence sings  
With well-labeled calm things,  
They assume it's too healthy to stink.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Resubmit in Ruin" icon="refresh-ccw">
They returned when the service looked cursed,  
With worse notes, louder users, and thirst.  
Then the board said, "At last,  
Now this feels like a blast."  
And approved what they'd punished at first.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Visible Enough" icon="file-warning">
There once was a fix, well-prepared,  
With a calm little risk note attached there.  
But till systems all smoked  
And the whole service choked,  
It was not an emergency, declared.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Proper Emergency" icon="shield-check">
A ticket submitted in haste,  
Was found to be cleanly encased.  
The board read the file,  
Reviewing the style,  
And deemed the emergency misplaced.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Suspicious Composure" icon="alert-circle">
The notes were devoid of a flaw,  
Which violated the governance law.  
A well-structured plea  
Is a terror to see,  
Deploy the armed guards to the draw.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Routine Devastation" icon="folder-open">
The server was burning quite bright,  
Which proved the deployment was right.  
The smoke in the hall,  
From the ash-covered wall,  
Ensured the compliance was tight.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Rubber Stamp Threshold" icon="stamp">
If documents look like a mess,  
We just give the button a press.  
A readable plan  
Goes into the can,  
It saves us procedural stress.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Orderly Rejection" icon="clipboard-x">
The rollback was documented well,  
With diagrams drafted to tell.  
The board read the text,  
And became quite perplexed,  
And denied the request as a shell.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Slightly Tilted Text" icon="alert-octagon">
A typo was found in the risk,  
A threat both profound and quite brisk.  
The board called a guard,  
And locked down the yard,  
And filed it away on a disk.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Queue Processed" icon="inbox">
The emergency entered the queue,  
With nothing whatever to do.  
We checked the first box,  
And adjusted the clocks,  
And deleted the rest of it too.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Form 4A" icon="file-minus">
The form for the crisis was blue,  
With sections for me and for you.  
It went to the tray,  
At the end of the day,  
And stayed there the whole weekend through.  
</Limerick>

```


## LIM-LLG-0389-AKL.mdx

_path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0389-AKL.mdx


path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0389-AKL.mdx
bytes: 2653
```markdown
---
title: Auxiliary Kitchen Labor Reclassified as Ceremonial Presence
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0389-akl
caseNumber: LLG-0389-AKL
date: 2026-05-15T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: memorial
subject: 'auxiliary kitchen labor, ceremonial presence, benevolence credit'
tableOfContents: false
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
description: >-
  Four hand-written limericks about retired casserole saints still getting the gratitude while somebody else hauls the potato salad.
relatedLorelog: "LLG-0389-AKL"
relatedMascots: ["sister-casserole-of-relief"]
concepts:
  - auxiliary-labor
  - lodge-kitchen
  - benevolence-credit
family: "benevolence"
---





<Limerick type="note" title="Potato Salad by Ancestry" icon="utensils">
Three chapters swore Gladys supplied  
The same potato dish, sanctified.  
She'd been retired for years,  
But in ledgerland, dears,  
Her mayonnaise still never died.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Who Brought the Tray" icon="tray">
The active ones lifted and baked,  
While the praise for the labor got faked.  
Someone else hauled the pan,  
But the record still ran  
On the saint whose casserole ached.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Tone Rather Than Fraud" icon="heart">
Treasurers looked at the split  
And decided it wasn't quite shit.  
Not fraud, just old grace  
Still attached to the place,  
Where the thanks outlived who carried it.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Cold Room Risk" icon="thermometer-snowflake">
They could fix who was thanked and repaid,  
But the whole hall might feel over-weighed.  
So they left warmth in place,  
Though it warped every case,  
For cold accuracy chills the buffet.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Same Salad Always" icon="file-minus">
The record says Gladys cooked this.  
The clerk didn't notice a miss.  
It's easier just  
To continue the trust,  
And leave the old name in abyss.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Ceremonial Contribution Tally" icon="file-digit">
The points were accrued to the old,  
As the database metrics foretold.  
The labor was moved,  
While the credit improved,  
And the ledger did just as it's told.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Mayonnaise Saints" icon="church">
The recipes morphed into prayer,  
And Gladys is permanently there.  
The kitchen relies  
On the saints who devise  
The salads of sacred despair.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Static Identity Marker" icon="tag">
The name on the record remained.  
The dish on the table was gained.  
The credit was stored  
On the usual board.  
The system is fully maintained.  
</Limerick>

```


## LIM-LLG-0389-MQM.mdx

_path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0389-MQM.mdx


path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0389-MQM.mdx
bytes: 2667
```markdown
---
title: 'Memorial Quorum Miscount, Esteem Presence Variant'
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0389-mqm
caseNumber: LLG-0389-MQM
date: 2026-05-15T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: esteem
subject: 'memorial quorum, esteem presence, threshold drift'
tableOfContents: false
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
description: >-
  Four hand-written limericks about a lodge spreadsheet counting the dead toward quorum because grief was imported as attendance.
relatedLorelog: "LLG-0389-MQM"
relatedMascots: ["sister-casserole-of-relief"]
concepts:
  - memorial-quorum
  - attendance-rot
  - threshold-drift
family: "other"
---





<Limerick type="note" title="Silent Voting Mass" icon="ghost">
They imported the dead with respect  
To keep names on the sheet and correct.  
But the quorum tool read  
Every ghost as "present" instead,  
And the roof vote got spiritually checked.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Enough History" icon="book-open">
The chair counted souls in continuity.  
The treasurer counted chairs in the room.  
One margin note sighed,  
"We've enough past to decide,  
But not enough asses for quorum by noon."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Respectful in Spreadsheet Form" icon="sheet">
No bastard was trying to cheat.  
They were mourning in tidy elite.  
But if grief fills the cells,  
Then arithmetic yells,  
"I don't know if this counts as a seat."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Re-heard on a Colder Day" icon="cloud-snow">
The guidance got icy at last:  
If the dead helped your motion get passed,  
You may honor the roll,  
But don't count every soul,  
Or re-hear that warm nonsense when winter blows past.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Quantitative Grief Event" icon="bar-chart">
The quorum parameters bent  
To log an emotional event.  
The dead voted "yea"  
In a procedural way,  
Authorizing the funds that we spent.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Valid Ethereal Attendance" icon="check-square">
The numbers assure us it's true:  
The dead are attending here too.  
The sheet is intact,  
Which establishes fact,  
So the roof will be patched up like new.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Attendance Status True" icon="server">
The software processed the array.  
The deceased were marked present today.  
The quorum was met  
By the standard we set.  
The meeting proceeded its way.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Unsanctioned Spiritual Voting" icon="shield-alert">
A ghost in the spreadsheet is wrong!  
The threat to the data is strong!  
The threshold of grief  
Needs a tactical brief  
Before the next structural song!  
</Limerick>

```


## LIM-LLG-0390-HAP.mdx

_path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0390-HAP.mdx


path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0390-HAP.mdx
bytes: 2615
```markdown
---
title: Memorial Roll Expanded to Include Honorary Absences
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0390-hap
caseNumber: LLG-0390-HAP
date: 2026-05-15T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: esteem
subject: 'honorary absences, memorial roll, quorum ambiguity'
tableOfContents: false
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
description: >-
  Four hand-written limericks about a lodge counting the absent with the dead and the present until nobody knew what quorum meant anymore.
relatedLorelog: "LLG-0390-HAP"
relatedMascots: ["peatworthy-abstention-clerk"]
concepts:
  - memorial-roll
  - quorum
  - chapter-elections
family: "other"
---





<Limerick type="note" title="Read Between the Dead" icon="book-heart">
At election, the secretary read  
The absent right in with the dead.  
The room murmured, "Hell,  
That is tender as well,  
But can tenderness chair us?" it said.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Spiritually Present" icon="ghost">
They were morally still in the hall,  
Though they had not been seen there at all.  
When the ballots came near,  
Folks got suddenly clear:  
"Can a ghost make the quorum?" and all.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Cruelty by Spreadsheet" icon="calculator">
No one wanted the minutes to show  
Who first told the estranged they could go.  
So they padded the roll  
With a spiritual poll,  
Which is warm till you need a hard "no."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Dignified Visibility" icon="users-round">
When a merger made bodies run thin,  
Honorary absences wandered right in.  
It's compassionate math:  
Keep esteem on the path  
Till the vote asks whose ass fills a chair.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Honorary Vote Threshold" icon="calculator">
The absent were tallied in full,  
Increasing the quorum's own pull.  
The officer seat  
Was declared incomplete  
By a metric impressively null.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Roll Call Bypass" icon="user-minus">
They weren't in the room for the vote.  
The clerk didn't care what he wrote.  
He counted them all  
In the empty old hall,  
And that is the end of the note.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Empty Seat Contingency" icon="siren">
A missing attendee is dire,  
A threat to the structural fire!  
Their spiritual mass  
Is required to pass,  
Lest the whole institution expire.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Ghostly Electorate" icon="scroll">
The names from the old vacant chairs  
Have taken to answering prayers.  
They sit in the hall  
Through the winter and fall,  
And manage the chapter's affairs.  
</Limerick>

```


## LIM-LLG-0390-KCL.mdx

_path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0390-KCL.mdx


path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0390-KCL.mdx
bytes: 2691
```markdown
---
title: 'Kitchen Credit Persistence Loop, Auxiliary Labor Afterlife'
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0390-kcl
caseNumber: LLG-0390-KCL
date: 2026-05-15T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: memorial
subject: 'kitchen credit, gratitude drift, auxiliary labor afterlife'
tableOfContents: false
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
description: >-
  Four hand-written limericks about beloved casserole elders still drawing the gratitude after new cooks did the actual hauling.
relatedLorelog: "LLG-0390-KCL"
relatedMascots: ["sister-casserole-of-relief"]
concepts:
  - auxiliary-labor
  - gratitude-drift
  - memorial-supper
family: "benevolence"
---





<Limerick type="note" title="Posthumous Payroll" icon="receipt">
The dish card still bore old Louise,  
Though she'd long since retired from peas.  
So the room gave her praise,  
And the ledger gave credit for days,  
In a very polite haunting, if you please.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Prepared By" icon="chef-hat">
Three statuses begged to be split:  
Who cooked it, whose card, whose dead wit.  
But the hall liked them blurred,  
So the labor deferred  
To nostalgia that billed by the bit.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Warmly Invisible" icon="eye-off">
The new cooks kept the suppers afloat,  
While the old names stayed loud in the note.  
That's the afterlife trick:  
Do the work, stay asterisked quick,  
While remembrance keeps clearing its throat.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Colder on the Table" icon="utensils-crossed">
The corrected cards looked a touch mean:  
Too precise for a fellowship scene.  
But if thanks track the dead  
While the living bake bread,  
Then your kindness is hiding a screen.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Posthumous Dish Accrual" icon="clipboard-list">
The database honors the dead  
By awarding them points for the bread.  
The living who bake  
Must submit for the sake  
Of the ghost who is presently fed.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Eternal Casserole Lineage" icon="flame">
Her name on the card became law,  
A legend of culinary awe.  
The dish makes itself  
On the physical shelf,  
A perpetual meal from the flaw.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Name Field Persistence" icon="minus">
The database copied the name.  
The serving remained much the same.  
The credit applied  
To the person who died.  
The record continues its frame.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Active Culinary Apparition" icon="ghost">
The ledger asserts she is there,  
Contributing meals from the chair.  
If the database yields  
Such robust data fields,  
Then the ghost is providing the fare.  
</Limerick>

```


## LIM-LLG-0391-LAA.mdx

_path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0391-LAA.mdx


path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0391-LAA.mdx
bytes: 2654
```markdown
---
title: Luncheon Assent Authorization Drift
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0391-laa
caseNumber: LLG-0391-LAA
date: 2026-05-15T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: boosterism
subject: 'luncheon assent, implied approval, procedural warmth'
tableOfContents: false
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
description: >-
  Four hand-written limericks about applause at lunch slowly hardening into budget approval because everybody seemed on board.
relatedLorelog: "LLG-0391-LAA"
relatedMascots: ["lionell-pancake-auditor"]
concepts:
  - luncheon-assent
  - civic-boosterism
  - grants-drift
family: "benevolence"
---





<Limerick type="note" title="Approved at Lunch" icon="badge-dollar-sign">
At luncheon they clapped for the plan,  
And someone wrote "done" with a hand.  
No motion. No sum.  
Just supportive warm hum.  
Then reimbursements came in like a band.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Paper Plate Consent" icon="plate">
The guidance got blessedly blunt:  
Don't confuse civic warmth with a grant.  
If they're nodding mid-bite  
With dry chicken in sight,  
That is not legal consent over lunch.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Reception Summary Drift" icon="arrow-down-up">
The clerk had two fields side by side:  
One for mood, one for what was applied.  
So "the room loved the pitch"  
Became budgetary switch,  
And the ledger developed a stride.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Fiscally Void" icon="x-circle">
Lionell, syrup-marked papers in tow,  
Said applause is not money, although  
It can help people cope  
And inflate civic hope.  
Just don't call it authorization flow.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Acoustic Funding Parameter" icon="file-audio">
An auditory spike from the floor  
Was logged as an opening door.  
The ledger was fed  
With the data instead,  
Thus granting the budget for more.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Lunch Input Parsed" icon="file-minus">
They cheered at the luncheon, we know,  
And the clerk made the budget just flow.  
The form had a space,  
So it went in that place,  
And the funds have decided to go.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Joy Classified As Currency" icon="badge-dollar-sign">
The applause at the table was loud,  
Which clearly meant funds from the crowd.  
The motion was heard  
Without saying a word,  
And the ledger is fiscally proud.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Unauthorized Joy Breach" icon="alert-triangle">
The noise in the room crossed the line  
And threatened the monetary spine.  
A smile from a guest  
Is a fiscal unrest,  
Which Lionell must firmly define.  
</Limerick>

```

```markdown
---
title: Ribbon Custody Dispute After Triple-Dedication Weekend
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0391-rcd

  - ribbon-cutting
  - artifact-custody
  - civic-legitimacy

<Limerick type="note" title="Three Albums, One Ribbon" icon="image">
A gold ribbon cut at a bakery,  
A riverside bench—and then bravery  
  At the industrial sign.  
  Three albums in line.  
All: "the original ribbon" in savory.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Either Or" icon="help-circle">
The reviewers concluded: either  
The ribbon had traveled hither  
  Faster than minutes—  
  Or civic business  
Had collapsed custody altogether.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Luncheon Sponsorship" icon="utensils">
The chamber argued: our lunch  
Confers primary custody's punch.  
  The service club: no—  
  Volunteer scissors bestow  
The operative claim on the bunch.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Behind the Sash" icon="camera">
The mayor's office maintained:  
Whichever ribbon the camera obtained  
  Behind the sash  
  In official flash—  
That's canonical for public stain.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Joint Seal" icon="lock">
The object now stores under joint  
Ownership seal, at the point  
  Where no one agreed  
  And everyone plead  
Prior rights. Three parties. One point.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Commemoratively Continuous" icon="infinity">
Public materials advised: say  
"Commemoratively continuous"—delay  
  The word "original."  
  But that virginal  
Phrase has already acquired its own display.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Narrative Convenience" icon="book">
Civic optimism collapsed  
Artifact custody into what grasped  
  Most cleanly: the story.  
  The ribbon's glory  
Was more about memory than clasped.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Cut Cleanly Each Time" icon="scissors">
The ribbon was cut without fault.  
Preservation staff took stock:  
  Continuity claimed  
  By memory—named  
As fabric length. But fabric's halt.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Acquiring Its Own Legitimacy" icon="star">
"Commemoratively continuous"—  
A phrase meant to be innocuous—  
  Began accruing  
  Its own ensuing  
Authority. Continuous and serious.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Three Sequences Not Clearly False" icon="check-square">
None of the photo sequences lied.  
All were accurate inside  
  Their own albuming.  
  The question: who's coming  
Forward when the same fabric's applied?  
</Limerick>
```

## LIM-LLG-0392-RCS.mdx

```markdown
---
title: Commemorative Ribbon Custody Schism
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0392-rcs
caseNumber: LLG-0392-RCS
date: 2026-05-15T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: custody
subject: 'ribbon custody, commemorative drift, artifact identity'
tableOfContents: false
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
description: >-
  Four hand-written limericks about one ceremonial ribbon becoming three separate originals because local memory preferred continuity over fabric facts.
relatedLorelog: "LLG-0392-RCS"
relatedMascots: ["ribbonward-cordialis"]
concepts:
  - ribbon-custody
  - artifact-identity
  - photo-proof
family: "benevolence"
---





<Limerick type="note" title="Three Originals" icon="ribbon">
One ribbon was somehow the first  
At three different events, unrehearsed.  
Each archive said, "Mine."  
The photos looked fine.  
So fabric got outvoted by thirst.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Aggressively Laminated" icon="laminate">
The dispute stayed polite for two weeks,  
Then got mean in municipal squeaks.  
Every claimant had proof,  
Yet exclusivity's spoof  
When the town wants one object to speak.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Save the Good Ribbon" icon="scissors">
One note said, "Save the good ribbon," and fled.  
Which explained approximately dread.  
Not whose opening day,  
Not whose plaque got the sway,  
Just that everyone worshipped one thread.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Shared Certainty" icon="briefcase">
So it rides in a padded valise,  
Under joint seal and rotating peace.  
If you force one true past,  
You lose three towns at last,  
So they archive shared longing, not peace.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Satin Triplicity" icon="ribbon">
The ribbon is one, but is three,  
A textile-based holy decree.  
It cut the new bank,  
The bench, and the tank,  
And bends all the laws of degree.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Shared Lamination" icon="file-badge">
We laminated it with care,  
To settle the three-way despair.  
Now nobody knows  
Where the heritage goes,  
But at least it’s not breathing the air.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Rotating Custody" icon="calendar">
The artifact schedule is set  
To cover the historical debt.  
If claimants agree  
On a rotational fee,  
The ledger can easily forget.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Padded Valise" icon="briefcase">
They put the damn thing in a case,  
So nobody loses their face.  
We rotate the key,  
For municipal glee,  
And hide the procedural waste.  
</Limerick>

```

```markdown
<Limerick type="note" title="Warmly Received" icon="hands-clapping">
The minutes said "warmly received,"  
Which the treasurer later believed  
Was a phrase that could spend.  
By the paperwork's end,  
No one knew what the room had conceived.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Courtesy-Adjacent" icon="wallet">
Three flavors of yes filled the hall:  
Funds approved, funds assumed, funds too kind to recall.  
Once gratitude's staged  
In a noon-crowded cage,  
Any clawback just sounds a bit small.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Atmospheric, Not Fiscal" icon="cloud">
The secretary swore with a wince,  
"Those remarks were atmospheric, gents."

</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Evenly Distributed Embarrassment" icon="balance">

The grants were too sweet to rescind.

<Limerick type="danger" title="Auditory Accounting" icon="volume">
The claps were assessed at a rate  
Of forty-five dollars a plate.  
We balanced the books  
On atmospheric looks  
And billed it all to the state.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Atmospheric Ledger" icon="banknote">
The room gave a moderate cheer,  
Which meant we spent funds for the year.  
It's too hard to track,  
So we're not asking back.  
The coffee is getting quite cold here.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Fiscal Handclap" icon="hands-clapping">
A single polite little clap  
Unleashed a financial mishap.  
We opened an inquiry  
With maximal fury,  
To cover the treasurer's gap.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Courtesy Obligation" icon="receipt">
The minutes recorded assent,  
Though nobody knew what it meant.  
With no clear receipt,  
The file is complete,  
And the money is officially spent.  
</Limerick>
```

```markdown
<Limerick type="note" title="Pride Must, Per Banner" icon="quote">

Is it enters the room pre-amazing.

<Limerick type="note" title="Decorative Legalities" icon="scissors">
We hoisted the banner for flair,

<Limerick type="danger" title="Unratified Stitches" icon="needle">

The meeting adjourned,  
The ledger returned,  
And nobody questioned the spin.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Operational Embroidery" icon="flag">
The thread had instructed the room.  
We filed it as "Loom-Given Doom."  
The clerk was concerned,  
The paragraphs burned,  
To manage the fabric's perfume.  
</Limerick>
```

```markdown
title: Resolution Banner Reinstated as Standing Policy

<Limerick type="note" title="Basement Recovery" icon="archive">
It came wrapped in obsolete raffle  
Notices and parade-clasp baffle—  
  Two sealed jars beside.  
  Across the lower side:  
A phrase that began to chafe, not waffle.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="No Vote Recorded" icon="x-circle">
No meeting book holds the vote  
That adopted the stitched note.  
  Yet officers had  
  Already been glad

</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Serve Visibly, Defer Gracefully" icon="eye">
"Serve visibly, defer gracefully"—  
The phrase aligned gracefully  
  With what they'd been doing.  
  Rediscovery: renewing,  
Not newly empowering. Faithfully.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Speaking Order" icon="list">
Within two weeks it had touched  
How they spoke at memorials—clutched  
  Succession order,  
  Public credit's border.  
The fabric held governance, much.

<Limerick type="note" title="Decorative Stitching" icon="scissors">

Decorative stitching cannot steer  
  Policy. The majority  
  Said: that's authority's  
Origin here—and has been, dear.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Most Durable Policy" icon="clock">
"Most durable policy arrives  
That way eventually"—derives  
  From the material  
  Before its burial.  
The majority vote: it survives.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Provisional Heritage Authority" icon="gavel">
It's listed now in the standing  
Resolutions ledger, outstanding  
  Under "provisional  
  Heritage"—divisional  
Legal force: none. Local: demanding.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="No Clear Legal Force" icon="shield-off">
Considerable local effect.  
No legal force to protect  
  Or override.  
  The phrase inside  
The bylaws: absent. Still checked.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Already Been Obeying It" icon="check">
Officers cited it as rediscovered  
Rather than newly discovered.  
  It had already shaped  
  The habits that draped  
Their customs—only now labeled, covered.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Archive Reads" icon="book-open">
The archive notes: a banner  
That shapes behavior without planner  
  Or formal adoption  
  Is a policy option  
Of the oldest and most stable manner.  
</Limerick>
```

```markdown
title: Parade Route Sanctification Drift

<Limerick type="note" title="Proper Procession Line" icon="map">
An old map from ninety-eight rose  
From a drawer full of folded old prose.  
Once they called it "the proper,"  
Permits mattered much softer,  
And detours were treated like foes.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Spiritually Irregular" icon="route">
The detour round roadwork looked wise,  
Till tradition got tears in its eyes.

Said adults in reflective supplies.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Banner Dignity" icon="shield">
They argued curb cuts were too thin  
For the banners' symbolic chagrin.

</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Too Practical to Photograph" icon="camera">
The case stayed deliciously stuck:  
Old routes simply looked more like luck.

As the year it got tamed,

<Limerick type="danger" title="Sacrosanct Pothole" icon="map-pin">
The detour was functionally sound,  
But heritage fiercely frowned.

And deployed the local bloodhound.

<Limerick type="danger" title="Geographic Filing Error" icon="folder">
The pavement was formally filed  
Under "Traditions of the Wild."  
When the ambulance came,  
We sorted its name  
And let it be properly exiled.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Asphalt Divination" icon="sparkles">
The map from the nineties became  
A scroll with a holy-like name.  
The crossing guard wept  
While the detour line slept  
And the asphalt accepted the blame.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Permit Displacement" icon="file-text">
The logical route was ignored,  
As old paper maps were adored.  
The binder was clear,  
The traffic was near,  
And the permit was slowly unmoored.  
</Limerick>
```

```markdown
  Four hand-written limericks about pancakes, projected goodwill, and scholarship money being counted in mood before dollars.
date: 2026-05-15T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: boosterism
subject: 'scholarship breakfast, forecast drift, civic boosterism'
tableOfContents: false
relatedLorelog: "LLG-0397-SBF"

concepts: ["pancake-breakfast", "scholarship-fund", "forecast-drift"]
family: 'benevolence'
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---





<Limerick type="note" title="Basically There" icon="utensils-crossed">
By ten-forty the emcee declared  
All four awards practically squared.  
The cashbox said, "Wait."  
But the crowd felt so great  
That the syrup got entered as shared.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Revenue-Adjacent Applause" icon="hands-clapping">
They treated applause as a fund,  
Like clapping could settle the sum.  
Unsold raffle strips  
Became generous tips,  
Till the cashbox said, "That's not how funds come."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Before the Second Spill" icon="droplets">
The guidance was crisp, after all:  
Don't announce every dream to the hall.  
If the second syrup spill  
Hasn't happened yet, chill.  
Mood is lovely, but mood won't clear all.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Laundered by Decency" icon="badge-dollar-sign">
Though enthusiasm spent past its means,  
Quiet donors came in from the wings.  
So the error got dressed  
As communal good sense,  
And the books wore benevolent jeans.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Syrup Level Threat" icon="alert-triangle">
The syrup dropped under the mark,  
Initiating an incident stark.  
Deploy the full team,  
To secure the whipped cream,  
And audit the flapjacks till dark.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Logged Mood" icon="file-digit">
The mood of the room was compiled,  
And placed in a folder and filed.  
The total was checked,  
The numbers connect,  
The data is cleanly exiled.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Forecasted Joy" icon="calculator">
The ledger projected a grin,  
Before the donations came in.  
The form requires cash,  
But we're making a dash,  
To deposit this excellent spin.  
</Limerick>
```

## LIM-LLG-0398-CCO.mdx

```markdown
---
title: Consolidated Chapter Office Continuity Loop
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0398-cco
caseNumber: LLG-0398-CCO
description: >-
  Four hand-written limericks about merged chapters retiring offices on paper and then letting those titles crawl back into power through etiquette.
date: 2026-05-15T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: continuity
subject: 'honorary office, merger drift, title persistence'
tableOfContents: false
relatedLorelog: "LLG-0398-CCO"
relatedMascots: ["311.eagleton-proclamation-clerk"]
concepts: ["merger-drift", "honorary-office", "chapter-governance"]
family: 'bin-8c'
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---





<Limerick type="note" title="Retired on Paper" icon="archive">
They retired old offices, neat,  
Then kept titles on banquet receipts.  
Three meetings went by,  
And "former" meant "why,  
Yes, of course they still steer from good seats."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Distributed into Tone" icon="speech">
The merger reduced not a thing.  
It just taught old authority to sing.  
Once the elders were named  
All objections got tamed,  
And politeness grew procedural sting.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="As a Former" icon="gavel">
The guidance grew blunt for a reason:  
If "As a former" arrives in due season,  
It may flavor the floor,  
But must not settle the score,  
Unless bylaws have finally stopped teasin'.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Calmer When Gently Obeyed" icon="armchair">
The room was more calm, it is true,  
When the elders got softly obeyed through.  
That's the trap of good tone:  
Soon no vote stands alone,  
And the chair learns to nod before you.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="The Phantom Veto" icon="ghost">
The office was strictly retired,  
Yet somehow it still isn't fired.  
The bylaws say nay,  
But etiquette's way,  
Has left the procedure acquired.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Seating Chart Violation" icon="siren">
A former chair sat in row three,  
A massive breach of decree!  
The protocol snaps,  
The merger collapsed,  
Because of a courtesy tea.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Properly Addressed" icon="mail">
The title of president died,  
So we placed it securely inside.  
The archive receipt,  
Has taken a seat,  
And voted to serve as a guide.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Existential Catering Threat" icon="siren">
A waiter who poured the hot tea,  
Said "President, sir" in row three.  
The bylaws collapsed,  
The timeline relapsed,  
And we locked down the whole registry.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Log Entry 82B" icon="file-text">
The former committee head spoke.  
No active procedure then broke.  
He finished his thought,  
The minutes were caught,  
And filed in the folder of oak.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Meeting Cycle Three" icon="coffee">
The elders are talking again.  
We wrote down the where and the when.  
They hold up the vote,  
I typed up the note,  
We'll pass it at quarter to ten.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The River Avenue Crown" icon="crown">
The title of North Annex Chief,  
Was filed underneath a motif.  
But now it commands,  
The folding of hands,  
And rules from the binder of grief.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Vector: As A Former" icon="bug">
The human who triggers the phrase,  
Will fracture the order for days.  
The system suspends,  
The logic upends,  
As etiquette blocks the displays.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Guidance Update 2.1" icon="clipboard">
The guidance was newly refined.  
All honorary ranks are declined.  
The seating array,  
Has zero to say,  
On votes that the chapter assigned.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Automotive Repair Log" icon="tool">
The former committee was loud,  
So maintenance serviced the crowd.  
The oil was drained,  
The chassis maintained,  
And protocol strictly allowed.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Booklet Title Crisis" icon="flame">
The booklet was printed in red,  
"To the Honorary Chair," it had said.  
We locked down the hall,  
And canceled the ball,  
To save the procedures from dread.  
</Limerick>

```
